Rita</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other storms of the same name, see <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Rita_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Rita (disambiguation)">Tropical Storm Rita (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rina" title="Hurricane Rina">Hurricane Rina</a>.</div>\n<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em;border-collapse:collapse;">\n<caption>Hurricane Rita</caption>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="display:none">\n<td colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Fatalities</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px">97\xe2\x80\x93125 total</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Damage</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px">$12 billion (2005 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Areas affected</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px"><a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region" title="Great Lakes region">Great Lakes region</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;">Part of the <b><a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005 Atlantic hurricane season</a></b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="display:none">\n<td colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hurricane Rita</b> was the fourth-most intense <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic tropical cyclone">Atlantic hurricane</a> ever recorded and the most intense <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> ever observed in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. Part of the record-breaking <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005 Atlantic hurricane season</a>, which included three of the top ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_intense_tropical_cyclones#North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="List of the most intense tropical cyclones">most intense Atlantic hurricanes</a> ever recorded (along with #1 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a> and #7 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a>), Rita was the seventeenth named storm, tenth hurricane, and fifth major hurricane of the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Atlantic hurricane season">season</a>. Rita formed near <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> on September&#160;18, 2005 that originally developed off the coast of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. It moved westward, and after passing through the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Straits" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Straits">Florida Straits</a>, Rita entered an environment of abnormally warm waters. Moving west-northwest, it <a href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid deepening">rapidly intensified</a> to reach peak winds of 180&#160;mph (290&#160;km/h), achieving Category 5 status on September&#160;21st. However, as Rita approached land through September 24, it weakened to a Category 3 and began to curve to the northwest, making landfall in Johnson\'s Bayou, Louisiana, between <a href="/wiki/Sabine_Pass,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabine Pass, Texas">Sabine Pass, Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holly_Beach,_Louisiana" title="Holly Beach, Louisiana">Holly Beach, Louisiana</a>, with winds of 120&#160;mph (190&#160;km/h). Rapidly weakening over land, Rita degenerated into a large <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a> over the lower <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Mississippi Valley">Mississippi Valley</a> by September&#160;26th.</p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, Rita\'s <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> inundated low-lying communities along the entire coast, worsening effects caused by Hurricane Katrina less than a month prior, such as topping the hurriedly-repaired Katrina-damaged <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">levees</a> at New Orleans. Parishes in Southwest Louisiana and counties in Southeast Texas where Rita made landfall suffered from catastrophic-to-severe flooding and wind damage. According to an October 25, 2005 Disaster Center report, 4,526 single-family dwellings were destroyed in Orange and Jefferson counties located in Southeast Texas. Major damage was sustained by 14,256 additional single-family dwellings, and another 26,211 single-family dwellings received minor damage. Mobile homes and apartments also sustained significant damage or total destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> In all, nine Texas counties and five Louisiana Parishes were declared <a href="/wiki/Disaster_area" title="Disaster area">disaster areas</a> after the storm. Electric service was <a href="/wiki/Power_outage" title="Power outage">disrupted</a> in some areas of both Texas and Louisiana for several weeks. Texas reported the most deaths from the hurricane, where 113&#160;deaths were reported, 107 of which were associated with the evacuation of the <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> metropolitan area.</p>\n<p>Moderate to severe damage was reported across the lower Mississippi Valley. Rainfall from the storm and its associated remnants extended from Louisiana to <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. Rainfall peaked at 16.00&#160;in (406&#160;mm) in Central Louisiana. Several <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> were also associated with the hurricane and its subsequent remnants. Throughout the path of Rita, damage totaled about $12&#160;billion (2005&#160;USD, $15.6&#160;billion 2017&#160;USD). As many as 120&#160;deaths in four U.S. states were directly related to the hurricane.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_2005_track.png" class="image"><img alt="The path of a tropical cyclone on a map as represented by colored dots. Each dot represents the storm\'s intensity at six-hour intervals." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Rita_2005_track.png/220px-Rita_2005_track.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Rita_2005_track.png/330px-Rita_2005_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Rita_2005_track.png/440px-Rita_2005_track.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="633" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_2005_track.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On September&#160;7, 2005, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> emerged off the west coast of Africa and moved westward into the Atlantic Ocean. Failing to produce organized, deep <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">atmospheric convection</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> the disturbance was not monitored by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a>&#160;(NHC) for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">tropical cyclogenesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TWOAT_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWOAT-3">[3]</a></sup> Convection associated with the system increased briefly late on September&#160;13 before dissipating shortly thereafter. At roughly the same time, a remnant surface <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> had developed from a dissipating <a href="/wiki/Stationary_front" title="Stationary front">stationary front</a> and began to drift westward north of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the tropical wave slowly became better organized and was first noted in the NHC\'s Tropical Weather Outlooks on September&#160;15 while northeast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TWO152123_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWO152123-4">[4]</a></sup> The wave merged with the surface trough two days later, triggering an increase in convective activity and organization. A subsequent decrease in <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> enabled for additional organization, and at 0000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on September&#160;18, the NHC estimated that the storm system had organized enough to be classified as a tropical depression,<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> the eighteenth disturbance during the <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">hurricane season</a> to do so. At the time, the disturbance, classified as Tropical Depression Eighteen,<sup id="cite_ref-ADV1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADV1-5">[5]</a></sup> was roughly 80&#160;mi (130&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a> and had developed <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">banding features</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DISC1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC1-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In generally favorable conditions for tropical development, the depression quickly organized, and attained <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> strength at 1800&#160;UTC that day based on data from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Hunters">reconnaissance flights</a> and nearby ships and <a href="/wiki/Weather_buoy" title="Weather buoy">weather buoys</a>. As a result, the tropical storm was named Rita.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DISC4_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC4-7">[7]</a></sup> However, an increase in moderate southerly vertical wind shear as the result of a nearby <a href="/wiki/Upper-level_low" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper-level low">upper-level low</a> subdued continued intensification and displaced convective activity to the north of Rita\'s center of circulation. Once the upper-level low weakened, Rita\'s center of circulation reformed to the north, compensating for the disorganization that resulted from the wind shear. Consequently, the tropical storm resumed its previous strengthening trend as it was steered westward across <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> along the south periphery of a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HURDAT_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Upon entering the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a> on September&#160;20, Rita strengthened into a Category&#160;1 hurricane by 1200&#160;UTC,<sup id="cite_ref-DISC11_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC11-9">[9]</a></sup> while maintaining a minimum <a href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> of 985&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 29.09&#160;<a href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" class="mw-redirect" title="Inches of mercury">inHg</a>). Six hours later, Rita intensified further into Category&#160;2 before subsequently passing approximately 45&#160;mi (72&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" title="Key West, Florida">Key West, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> Aided by a favorable <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> pattern and anomalously warm <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a>&#160;(SSTs), the trend of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> continued,<sup id="cite_ref-DISC11_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC11-9">[9]</a></sup> and Rita reached Category&#160;3 status upon entering the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> by 0600&#160;UTC on September&#160;21, making it a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HURDAT_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF" class="image"><img alt="Colorized satellite image of a tropical cyclone. Bluer colors indicate areas of warmer cloud tops, indicative of marginal convective activity; redder and whiter colors indicate areas of colder cloud tops, indicating stronger convective activity." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF/220px-Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF/330px-Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF/440px-Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="400" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita2005-colorIR2.GIF" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nInfrared image of Hurricane Rita at peak intensity on September&#160;21</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Once in the Gulf of Mexico, Rita passed over the extremely warm <a href="/wiki/Loop_Current" title="Loop Current">Loop Current</a> during the midday hours of September&#160;21, enabling continued strengthening. As a result, the hurricane\'s wind field significantly expanded and the storm\'s barometric pressure quickly fell.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> By 1800&#160;UTC that day, Rita attained <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">Category&#160;5 hurricane</a> intensity,<sup id="cite_ref-DISC17_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC17-10">[10]</a></sup> the highest category on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SSHWS_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSHWS-11">[11]</a></sup> Favorable conditions allowed for additional development, and at 0300&#160;UTC on September&#160;22, Rita reached its peak intensity with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 180&#160;mph (285&#160;km/h) and a minimum barometric pressure of 895&#160;mbar (hPa; 26.43&#160;inHg), making it the strongest <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> ever recorded in the Gulf of Mexico. At the time, it was located 310&#160;mi (500&#160;km) south of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Delta" title="Mississippi River Delta">Mississippi River Delta</a>.</p>\n<p>Rita maintained Category&#160;5 hurricane intensity for 18&#160;hours before an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> took place, weakening the hurricane to Category&#160;4 intensity by 1800&#160;UTC on September&#160;22. At the same time, the tropical cyclone began to curve northwestward around the southwestern periphery of a ridge of high pressure over the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">Southeastern United States</a>. As a result of the cycle, a new, larger <a href="/wiki/Eyewall" class="mw-redirect" title="Eyewall">eyewall</a> consolidated, resulting in Rita\'s wind field expanding. Due to wind shear and cooler <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a> waters, the hurricane continued to weaken, contrary to typical tropical cyclone processes that occur after eyewall replacement cycles. Rita weakened to Category&#160;3 strength before making <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> at 0740&#160;UTC on September&#160;24 in extreme southwestern <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> between <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Bayou,_Louisiana" title="Johnson Bayou, Louisiana">Johnson Bayou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sabine_Pass" title="Sabine Pass">Sabine Pass</a>. At the time of landfall, Rita was a Category&#160;3&#160;hurricane with winds of 120&#160;mph (190&#160;km/h) and a barometric pressure of 937&#160;mbar (hPa; 27.67&#160;inHg).<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Once inland on September&#160;24, Rita began to rapidly weaken.<sup id="cite_ref-DISC29_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC29-12">[12]</a></sup> The tropical cyclone had been downgraded to tropical storm intensity nearly 12&#160;hours after landfall. Proceeding northward roughly parallel to the state border between Louisiana and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Weather_radar" title="Weather radar">radar imagery</a> indicated that the storm soon lacked winds of tropical storm-force. Therefore, the NHC classified the system as a tropical depression while it was over <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> by 0600&#160;UTC on September&#160;25,<sup id="cite_ref-DISC30_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC30-13">[13]</a></sup> shortly before it turned northeastward ahead of an approaching <a href="/wiki/Weather_front" title="Weather front">frontal boundary</a>. Early the next day, the depression lost much of its convection over southeastern <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, and degenerated into a remnant low by 0600&#160;UTC that day. The frontal boundary subsequently absorbed the remaining system six hours later over the southern <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahamas">Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Satellite image of a rather weak tropical cyclone - the storm is an elongated mass of clouds, stretching horizontally." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg/220px-TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg/330px-TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg/440px-TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4500" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TS_Rita_18_sept_2005_1540Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTropical Storm Rita over the eastern Bahamas on September&#160;18</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>At 0300&#160;<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on September&#160;18, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm warning</a> was issued for the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a> and the Southeast and Central <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>. At the same time, a <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane watch">hurricane watch</a> was also issued for the northwest Bahamas. By 0600&#160;UTC the following day, the hurricane watch was upgraded to a hurricane warning for the northwest Bahamas excluding <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco Islands</a> which were later put under a tropical storm warning. Several hours later, a hurricane warning was issued for <a href="/wiki/Exuma" title="Exuma">Exuma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andros_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Andros Island">Andros Island</a>. At 1800&#160;UTC, the tropical storm warning for the Turks and Caicos was discontinued as the threat from Rita diminished. This discontinuation later included the southeast Bahamas. By 1500&#160;UTC on September&#160;20, all watches and warnings for the islands were discontinued as Rita moved into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> Residents in the Bahamas were urged to board up their homes and stock up on emergency supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-RO2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RO2-14">[14]</a></sup> At least one shelter was opened and schools throughout the country were closed.<sup id="cite_ref-CDERA1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDERA1-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nassau_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Nassau International Airport">Nassau International Airport</a> was also closed due to the storm on September&#160;19 and would remain closed until the evening of September&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Officials in Cuba warned residents of possible impacts from Rita and closed public facilities in northern areas. Some evacuations took place in villages near the northern coastline and several shelters were opened.<sup id="cite_ref-CMR1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMR1-17">[17]</a></sup> An estimated 150,000 people were evacuated in northern Cuba ahead of the storm. About 600 shelters were opened in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> which could house a total of 120,000 people. In western Cuba, more than 42,000 were given shelter in Matanzas, 31,000 in Villa Claro and 6,300 in Sancti Spiritus.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In Havana, power was turned off at noon on September&#160;19 to protect transformers, this also led to the disruption of natural gas lines.<sup id="cite_ref-RWCuba_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWCuba-19">[19]</a></sup> A large-scale preparation was put in place by the Ministry of Health in Cuba. A total of 14,859 medical personnel were mobilized to quickly assist residents impacted by Rita. The personnel consisted of 3,767 doctors, 5,143 nurses, 2,139 specialists, 1,072 health officials, and 2,738 other staff members. A total of 519 vehicles were also mobilized; it included 241 ambulances, 36 trucks, 21 panels, and 221 other vehicles. Throughout northern Cuba, a total of 1,486 shelters were opened, most of which were filled during the evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Satellite image of a strengthening hurricane passing between two landmasses. The hurricane has also developed an eye." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg/220px-Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg" width="220" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg/330px-Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg/440px-Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5600" data-file-height="7200" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_9-20-05_1835UTC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Rita as a <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 2 hurricane</a> crossing the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Florida Straits</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On September&#160;18, when Rita was declared a tropical storm, phased evacuations began in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>. All tourists were told to evacuate the Lower Keys immediately and residents in mobile homes were told to prepare to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-RO1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RO1-21">[21]</a></sup> By September&#160;20, mandatory evacuations were in place for the 80,000 residents of the Keys. Both lanes on <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_(Florida)" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 1 (Florida)">Route 1</a> were directed northbound to speed up evacuations. City busses picked up those who did not have transportation out of the Keys. An estimated 2.3&#160;million people in <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami-Dade County</a> were warned about the possibility of a direct hit on <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> and told to prepare to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-TA1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TA1-22">[22]</a></sup> A State of Emergency was declared ahead of Rita later that day by President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. This would allow federal assistance to aid the affected areas in the wake of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-FEMAFL1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FEMAFL1-23">[23]</a></sup> Throughout Florida, a total of 340,000 people were placed under mandatory or voluntary evacuation orders.<sup id="cite_ref-SP1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SP1-24">[24]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Five shelters were opened in southern Florida with a total capacity of 4,335 people. Tolls on northbound roads were lifted in <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">Monroe County</a>. A total of four hospitals, three assisted living facilities, and two nursing homes were evacuated. Military support in the form of 7,000 soldiers, eight <a href="/wiki/UH-60_Black_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="UH-60 Black Hawk">Black Hawk helicopters</a>, two <a href="/wiki/CH-47_Chinook" class="mw-redirect" title="CH-47 Chinook">Chinook helicopters</a>, three <a href="/wiki/OH-58_Kiowa" class="mw-redirect" title="OH-58 Kiowa">Kiowa helicopters</a>, one <a href="/wiki/C-12_Huron" class="mw-redirect" title="C-12 Huron">Huron aircraft</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short 360 aircraft</a>, one <a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">Hercules aircraft</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/C-26_Metroliner" class="mw-redirect" title="C-26 Metroliner">Metroliner aircraft</a> was provided. A task force was put on standby in <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Joint_Air_Reserve_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Homestead Joint Air Reserve Base">Homestead Joint Air Reserve Base</a> to quickly deploy in affected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-SR3_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR3-25">[25]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a> prepared food to deliver to affected areas after Rita. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> deployed personnel to coordinate evacuations. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="United States Department of Health and Human Services">United States Department of Health and Human Services</a> sent fully equipped medical teams and supplies if needed. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">United States Department of Homeland Security</a> pre-positioned over 100 trucks of ice and packed food to deliver following Rita. Two helicopters and one <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne_aircraft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cheyenne aircraft (page does not exist)">Cheyenne aircraft</a> were also provided to assist with recovery efforts. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">United States Department of the Interior</a> shut down all national parks in Florida and evacuated workers in low-lying areas.<sup id="cite_ref-FEMAFL2_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FEMAFL2-26">[26]</a></sup> Military cargo planes evacuated hospital patients from three acute-care hospitals in the Keys.<sup id="cite_ref-RO3_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RO3-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On Tuesday Sept. 20th, Louisiana Governor Kathleen Blanco issued a state of emergency for all parishes in the southwestern region of Louisiana, and requested in writing of President George W. Bush that he issue a federal state of emergency for the entire state. Refugees still at the New Orleans Convention Center and Superdome were being evacuated as a precaution, and national guard troops and other emergency personnel in for the Hurricane Katrina aftermath were being mobilized to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Select military personnel stayed in New Orleans for Hurricane Rita including Task Force California (2-185 Armor and 1-184 Infantry).<sup id="cite_ref-184_Katrina1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184_Katrina1-29">[29]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-184_Katrina2_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184_Katrina2-30">[30]</a></sup></p>\n<p>By the morning of Wednesday Sept. 21st, as Rita\'s strength, course and speed became clearer, officials of <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">Cameron Parish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calcasieu_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana">Calcasieu Parish</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Jefferson Davis Parish, Louisiana">Jefferson Davis Parish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadia_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Acadia Parish, Louisiana">Acadia Parish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Parish" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Parish">Iberia Parish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beauregard_Parish" class="mw-redirect" title="Beauregard Parish">Beauregard Parish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermillion_Parish" class="mw-redirect" title="Vermillion Parish">Vermillion Parish</a> began to strongly encourage residents to evacuate ahead of the storm, with a 6:00 PM Thursday deadline set. Most residents followed the recommendations of their respective officials, hitting the road by the deadline, though many returned home and waited until early the next morning after encountering severe traffic delays. Southern Cameron Parish residents, used to frequent evacuations, were gone by noon on Thursday; when parish officials returned to the Hwy. 27 "Gibbstown Bridge" that crosses the Intracoastal Canal into Lower Cameron Parish two days later in preparation of damage inspection and rescue of any stranded and/or injured residents, no one was known to have remained.<sup id="cite_ref-184_Katrina1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184_Katrina1-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas">Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stranded_on_Highway_60.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Stranded_on_Highway_60.jpg/220px-Stranded_on_Highway_60.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2c/Stranded_on_Highway_60.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="213" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stranded_on_Highway_60.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMotorists stranded on <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_60" title="Texas State Highway 60">Highway 60</a> during Hurricane Rita evacuation.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Rick_Perry" title="Rick Perry">Rick Perry</a> recalled all emergency personnel, including almost 1,200 <a href="/wiki/Texas_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas National Guard">Texas National Guard</a>, 1,100 <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Guard" title="Texas State Guard">Texas State Guard</a>, and several hundred Texas Game Wardens from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a> recovery efforts in anticipation of Hurricane Rita\'s arrival. In addition, the Federal Government deployed 11 Disaster Medical Assistance Teams (DMATs),<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> staging them in mobile field hospitals across eastern Texas. The teams treated 7500 patients during the response.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coastal_Evacuations_in_Texas_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coastal_Evacuations_in_Texas-33">[33]</a></sup> On September 22, Governor Perry and the Texas Department of Transportation implemented a <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">contraflow lane reversal</a> on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">Interstate 45</a> north towards <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">Interstate 10</a> west towards <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_290" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Highway 290">U.S. Highway 290</a> northwest to <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gridlock_in_Houston_as_Texans_Flee_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gridlock_in_Houston_as_Texans_Flee-34">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As part of the evacuation, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a> in Houston handed off control of the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> to their <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">Russian</a> counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Concerns had been raised over the state of the oil industry in response to Rita. The storm threatened a large amount of oil infrastructure that was left undamaged by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oil_companies_prep_for_hurricane.2C_prices_drop_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oil_companies_prep_for_hurricane.2C_prices_drop-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Texas_Coastal_Bend" title="Texas Coastal Bend">Texas Gulf Coast</a> is home to 23% of the United States\' refining capacity, and numerous offshore production platforms were in Rita\'s path.<sup id="cite_ref-Big_Oil_Braces_for_Rita_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Oil_Braces_for_Rita-37">[37]</a></sup> A direct strike on Houston could disable more than a quarter of the United States\' fuel-making capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Valero_Energy_Corp" class="mw-redirect" title="Valero Energy Corp">Valero Energy Corp</a>, the nation\'s largest refiner, stated on September 21 that Rita could have caused gasoline prices to rise well above <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>3 per US <a href="/wiki/Gallon" title="Gallon">gallon</a> ($0.79/L), at a time when the U.S. average price was $2.77/gal.<sup id="cite_ref-Rita_shuts_down_US_refineries_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rita_shuts_down_US_refineries-39">[39]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_evacuation">Mass evacuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mass evacuation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Just three weeks after Hurricane Katrina devastated the northern Gulf Coast, the threat of yet another major hurricane prompted mass evacuations in coastal Texas. An estimated 2.5&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 3.7&#160;million people fled prior to Rita\'s landfall,<sup id="cite_ref-TXHroReport_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TXHroReport-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EvacDeaths_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EvacDeaths-41">[41]</a></sup> making it one of the largest evacuations in United States\' history.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Officials in <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">Galveston County</a> (which includes the city of <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston</a>), which was devastated by the <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Hurricane_of_1900" class="mw-redirect" title="Galveston Hurricane of 1900">Galveston Hurricane of 1900</a>, ordered mandatory evacuations, effective September 21 at 6 p.m., in a staggered sequence. Officials designated geographical zones in the area to facilitate an orderly evacuation. People were scheduled to leave at different times over a 24-hour period depending on the zone in which the people were located. The scheduled times were set well in advance of the storm\'s possible landfall later in the week, but not soon enough to ensure that all residents could evacuate safely in advance of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror-42">[42]</a></sup> Nonetheless, many residents remained in the county because they were either unaware of the danger of the storm or believed that it was more important to protect their belongings, particularly in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">looting</a> following Hurricane Katrina.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The evacuation included transfer of all inpatients from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">University of Texas Medical Branch</a> hospital to other regional hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> 400 patients were prisoners under the ward of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Department_of_Criminal_Justice" title="Texas Department of Criminal Justice">Texas Department of Criminal Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> These patients were systematically transferred to the University of Texas Health Center at Tyler.<sup id="cite_ref-Texas_Colleges_Ready_for_Rita.2C_as_Some_of_Katrina.27s_Academic_Evacuees_Are_Uprooted_Again_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Texas_Colleges_Ready_for_Rita.2C_as_Some_of_Katrina.27s_Academic_Evacuees_Are_Uprooted_Again-46">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Officials of Harris County hoped that the designation of zones A, B, and C would help prevent bottlenecks in traffic leaving the area similar to those seen at New Orleans prior to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis" title="Hurricane Dennis">Hurricane Dennis</a> earlier that year.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Also, people in certain zones were to be forced to go to certain cities in Texas and were not allowed to exit their designated routes except for food and gas&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 another feature of the evacuation plan which officials hoped would keep traffic flow orderly.</p>\n<p>The evacuation-destination cities included <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/College_Station,_Texas" title="College Station, Texas">College Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Texas" title="Huntsville, Texas">Huntsville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lufkin,_Texas" title="Lufkin, Texas">Lufkin</a>, Texas. Evacuees were asked to try hotels in the <a href="/wiki/Midland,_Texas" title="Midland, Texas">Midland</a>/<a href="/wiki/Odessa,_Texas" title="Odessa, Texas">Odessa</a> area when hotels began to sell out in other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On Wednesday, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> mayor <a href="/wiki/Bill_White_(Texas_politician)" title="Bill White (Texas politician)">Bill White</a> urged residents to evacuate the city, telling residents, "Don\'t wait; the time for waiting is over," reminding residents of the disaster in New Orleans.<sup id="cite_ref-Miles_of_Traffic_as_Texans_Heed_Order_to_Leave_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miles_of_Traffic_as_Texans_Heed_Order_to_Leave-49">[49]</a></sup> After heavy traffic snarled roads leading out of town and gas shortages left numerous vehicles stranded, Mayor White backed off his earlier statement with, "If you\'re not in the evacuation zone, follow the news," advising people to use common sense.<sup id="cite_ref-Miles_of_Traffic_as_Texans_Heed_Order_to_Leave_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miles_of_Traffic_as_Texans_Heed_Order_to_Leave-49">[49]</a></sup> However, by 3:00&#160;p.m. that afternoon, the freeway system in Houston was at a stand-still.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To the east of Houston, officials had set up evacuation routes in response to the slow evacuation of residents prior to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lili" title="Hurricane Lili">Hurricane Lili</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> During the Rita evacuation, these preparations and their execution were overwhelmed by the enormous and unprecedented number of people fleeing from the Houston area prior to the departure of local residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror-42">[42]</a></sup> By the time <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Texas" title="Jefferson County, Texas">Jefferson County</a> began their mandatory evacuation, local roads were already full of Houstonians.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Traffic on designated evacuation routes was forced to go far slower than the speeds experienced with any previous hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>\n<p>By late Thursday (22nd) morning, the <a href="/wiki/Contraflow" class="mw-redirect" title="Contraflow">contraflow</a> lanes had been ordered opened after officials determined that the state\'s highway system had become <a href="/wiki/Gridlock" title="Gridlock">gridlocked</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The Texas Department of Transportation was unprepared to execute such a large-scale evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Coordination and implementation of the contraflow plan took 8 to 10 hours as inbound traffic was forced to exit. Police were stationed to assist with traffic flow. Evacuees fought traffic Wednesday afternoon through mid-day Friday, moving only a fraction of the normal distance expected.<sup id="cite_ref-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror-42">[42]</a></sup> Average travel times to Dallas were 24\xe2\x80\x9336 hours, travel times to Austin were 12\xe2\x80\x9318 hours and travel times to San Antonio were 10\xe2\x80\x9316 hours, depending on the point of departure in Houston.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Many motorists ran out of gas or experienced breakdowns in temperatures that neared 100&#160;\xc2\xb0F (38&#160;\xc2\xb0C). Traffic volumes did not ease for nearly 48 hours as more than three million residents evacuated the area in advance of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evacuation_worked.2C_but_created_a_highway_horror-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Evacuation_deaths">Evacuation deaths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Evacuation deaths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As an estimated 2.5&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 3.7&#160;million people evacuated the Texas coastline, a significant <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat wave</a> affected the region. The combination of severe gridlock and excessive heat led to between 90 and 118 deaths even before the storm arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-TXHroReport_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TXHroReport-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EvacDeaths_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EvacDeaths-41">[41]</a></sup> Reports from the <i><a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">Houston Chronicle</a></i> indicated 107 evacuation-related fatalities. <a href="/wiki/Texas_Legislature" title="Texas Legislature">Texas Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Garnet_Coleman" title="Garnet Coleman">Garnet Coleman</a> criticized the downplay of the deaths in the evacuation and questioned whether the storm would be deadlier than the preparations.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> According to local officials, the traffic reached a point where residents felt safer riding out the storm at home rather than being stuck in traffic when Rita struck.<sup id="cite_ref-TXHroReport_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TXHroReport-40">[40]</a></sup> Many evacuees periodically turned off their air conditioning to reduce fuel consumption as well as drank less water to limit the number of "restroom stops." According to a post-storm study, which reported 90 evacuation-related deaths, nine people perished solely as a result of <a href="/wiki/Hyperthermia" title="Hyperthermia">hyperthermia</a>. However, it was suspected that most of the 67 deaths attributed to heat stress were a combination of hyperthermia and chronic health conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-EvacDeaths_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EvacDeaths-41">[41]</a></sup> In addition to the heat-related deaths, 23 nursing home evacuees were killed after a bus caught fire on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">Interstate 45</a> near <a href="/wiki/Wilmer,_Texas" title="Wilmer, Texas">Wilmer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EvacDeaths_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EvacDeaths-41">[41]</a></sup> The bus erupted into flames after the vehicle\'s rear <a href="/wiki/Axle" title="Axle">axle</a> overheated, due to insufficient lubrication, and ignited <a href="/wiki/Therapeutic_oxygen" class="mw-redirect" title="Therapeutic oxygen">therapeutic oxygen</a> tanks on board.<sup id="cite_ref-BusSettlement_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusSettlement-59">[59]</a></sup> According to a resident near the site of the accident, there were three explosions.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Many of the passengers were mobility-impaired making escape difficult or impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In June 2009, nearly four years after the fire, families of those who died in the accident won an $80&#160;million settlement against the manufacturer of the bus and the company that provided the nursing home with it.<sup id="cite_ref-BusSettlement_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusSettlement-59">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita_tornado_outbreak" title="Hurricane Rita tornado outbreak">Hurricane Rita tornado outbreak</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_2005_rainfall.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rita_2005_rainfall.gif/220px-Rita_2005_rainfall.gif" width="220" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rita_2005_rainfall.gif/330px-Rita_2005_rainfall.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rita_2005_rainfall.gif/440px-Rita_2005_rainfall.gif 2x" data-file-width="830" data-file-height="912" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rita_2005_rainfall.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Rita Rainfall</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In some areas, the effects of Hurricane Rita were not nearly as severe as anticipated. The <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> feared in Galveston and Houston struck farther east as the storm\'s center came ashore at the Louisiana border. Winds blowing offshore in Texas actually flattened the surge, which was only 7 feet (2.1&#160;m) in Galveston, well below the height of the <a href="/wiki/Seawall" title="Seawall">seawall</a>. The 5 inches (130&#160;mm) of rain expected to fall overnight in New Orleans as Rita came ashore also did not happen, and the pressure on the levee system was eased. Still, a storm surge of up to 18 feet (5.5&#160;m) struck southwestern Louisiana, and coastal parishes experienced extensive damage. In <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">Cameron Parish</a>, the communities of <a href="/wiki/Holly_Beach,_Louisiana" title="Holly Beach, Louisiana">Holly Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hackberry,_Louisiana" title="Hackberry, Louisiana">Hackberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameron,_Louisiana" title="Cameron, Louisiana">Cameron</a>, Creole and Grand Chenier were essentially destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_Review_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Review-62">[62]</a></sup> There were also severe impacts, mainly due to wind, in inland parishes and counties across <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Louisiana" title="Southwest Louisiana">Southwest Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Texas" title="Southeast Texas">Southeast Texas</a>, respectively. Cities such as <a href="/wiki/Beaumont,_Texas" title="Beaumont, Texas">Beaumont, Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Charles,_Louisiana" title="Lake Charles, Louisiana">Lake Charles, Louisiana</a>, as well as surrounding communities, suffered extensive wind damage.</p>\n<p>An estimated two million people lost <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Benfield_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benfield-63">[63]</a></sup> Total damage is estimated at approximately $12&#160;billion, making Rita the tenth-costliest storm in U.S. history.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deaths">Deaths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Deaths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox bordered" style="width: 250px; font-size: 95%; float: right; clear:right;" cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0">\n<tr>\n<th>State</th>\n<th>State total</th>\n<th>County/Parish</th>\n<th>Reported<br />\ndeaths</th>\n<th>Direct<br />\ndeaths</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a></td>\n<td rowspan="2" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><b>2</b>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-WKRN_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WKRN-64">[64]</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Escambia_County,_Florida" title="Escambia County, Florida">Escambia</a></td>\n<td>1<sup id="cite_ref-WKRN_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WKRN-64">[64]</a></sup></td>\n<td>1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Walton_County,_Florida" title="Walton County, Florida">Walton</a></td>\n<td>1<sup id="cite_ref-WKRN_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WKRN-64">[64]</a></sup></td>\n<td>1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a></td>\n<td rowspan="1" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><b>1</b>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-WKRN_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WKRN-64">[64]</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Calcasieu_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana">Calcasieu</a></td>\n<td>1<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n<td>1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a></td>\n<td rowspan="2" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><b>4</b>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-65">[65]</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Humphreys_County,_Mississippi" title="Humphreys County, Mississippi">Humphreys</a></td>\n<td>1<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-66">[66]</a></sup></td>\n<td>1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Pike_County,_Mississippi" title="Pike County, Mississippi">Pike</a></td>\n<td>3<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="9" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a></td>\n<td rowspan="9" bgcolor="#E6E9FF"><b>113</b>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-65">[65]</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Angelina_County,_Texas" title="Angelina County, Texas">Angelina</a></td>\n<td>2<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></td>\n<td>1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dallas_County,_Texas" title="Dallas County, Texas">Dallas</a></td>\n<td>23<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-65">[65]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">Galveston</a></td>\n<td>36<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">Harris</a></td>\n<td>35<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-70">[70]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Texas" title="Jefferson County, Texas">Jefferson</a></td>\n<td>6<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Liberty_County,_Texas" title="Liberty County, Texas">Liberty</a></td>\n<td>2<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></td>\n<td>2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Texas" title="Montgomery County, Texas">Montgomery</a></td>\n<td>2<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-70">[70]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Shelby_County,_Texas" title="Shelby County, Texas">Shelby</a></td>\n<td>1<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Walker_County,_Texas" title="Walker County, Texas">Walker</a></td>\n<td>5<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr bgcolor="#E6E9FF">\n<td>Totals</td>\n<td><b>120</b>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><b>120</b></td>\n<td><b>7</b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="small">\n<td colspan="5">Because of differing sources, totals may not match.</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The reported death toll for Hurricane Rita was 120. Only seven were direct deaths. One was caused by a tornado spawned in the storm\'s outer bands, one was due to storm surge flooding and three others were caused by trees blown down in the storm. The two Florida deaths both occurred in <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">rip currents</a> caused by Rita\'s distant waves.</p>\n<p>Direct deaths are those caused by the direct effects of the <a href="/wiki/Winds" class="mw-redirect" title="Winds">winds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flooding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tornadoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tornadoes">tornadoes</a>, storm surge or <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">oceanic</a> effects of Rita. Indirect deaths are caused by hurricane-related accidents (including <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">car</a> accidents, <a href="/wiki/Crime" title="Crime">crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">fires</a> or other incidents), cleanup and evacuation incidents and health issues (such as <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Illness">illnesses</a>, lack of emergency aid).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean">Caribbean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Caribbean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As Rita developed near the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, it dropped up to 5&#160;in (130&#160;mm) of rain but caused little damage. Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, swells produced by Rita reached 10&#160;ft (3.0&#160;m) and storm surge was estimated at 3 to 5&#160;ft (0.91 to 1.52&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Strong winds were reported across the islands, but no damage resulted from the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In Cuba, Rita produced winds up to 65&#160;mph (105&#160;km/h) and more than 5&#160;in (127&#160;mm) of rain in some areas. This resulted in significant structural damage but no loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-RWCuba_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWCuba-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC1-78">[78]</a></sup> In the Bay Shore area of Havana, water levels rose and inundated 20 blocks of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-RWCuba_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWCuba-19">[19]</a></sup> An estimated 400,000 people in the city lost power a result of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-CC1_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CC1-79">[79]</a></sup> In a two-hour span, more than 8.2 inches (210&#160;mm) of rain fell in <a href="/wiki/Bauta,_Cuba" title="Bauta, Cuba">Bauta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The torrential rains led to 34 homes collapsing in Havana. Storm surge produced by Rita penetrated an estimated 330&#160;ft (100&#160;m) inland, flooding several towns.<sup id="cite_ref-CC1_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CC1-79">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_2">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Rita produced moderate rains across southern <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, peaking at 5.13 inches (130&#160;mm) in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tenraw,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tenraw, Florida (page does not exist)">Tenraw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> A band of rain, estimated to be 20&#160;mi (32&#160;km) wide produced heavier rain, with doppler radar estimating some totals over 10 inches (250&#160;mm).<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL1_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL1-81">[81]</a></sup> Most of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> received 3&#160;in (76.2&#160;mm) of rain or more. The <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">highest sustained winds</a> were recorded at 20:32&#160;<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> (3:32&#160;p.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a>) on September&#160;20 in <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a> at 62&#160;mph (100&#160;km/h). Gusts in Key West were recorded at 76&#160;mph (122&#160;km/h). A maximum storm surge of 5&#160;ft (1.5&#160;m) was recorded,<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> which flooded at least 200 homes throughout four blocks in Key West.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL2_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL2-82">[82]</a></sup> Floodwaters up to 3&#160;ft (0.91&#160;m) deep reached the runways at <a href="/wiki/Key_West_International_Airport" title="Key West International Airport">Key West International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> A storm surge of 1.5&#160;ft (0.46&#160;m) was recorded in Miami, although no flooding was reported. Minor erosion also occurred on south-facing beaches. At the height of the storm, an estimated 126,000 people were without power.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL1_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL1-81">[81]</a></sup> One <a href="/wiki/Funnel_cloud" title="Funnel cloud">funnel cloud</a> was reported along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">Interstate 95</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Worth,_Florida" title="Lake Worth, Florida">Lake Worth</a>. Winds were estimated at 30\xe2\x80\x9340&#160;mph (48\xe2\x80\x9364&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL3_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL3-83">[83]</a></sup> High seas from Rita on September&#160;22 flooded parts of coastal <a href="/wiki/Walton_County,_Florida" title="Walton County, Florida">Walton County</a>. Moderate beach erosion also occurred as a result of the high seas. Damages from the flooding estimated at $200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL4_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL4-84">[84]</a></sup> Damages in southern Florida were minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> On September&#160;24, strong rip currents produced by the remnants of Rita resulted in the death of one person near <a href="/wiki/Miramar_Beach,_Florida" title="Miramar Beach, Florida">Miramar Beach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCFL5_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCFL5-85">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana_2">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Rita&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2883" data-file-height="1869" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_16669_-_Photograph_by_Win_Henderson_taken_on_10-03-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Holly_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Holly Beach">Holly Beach</a>, a town along the Gulf Coast completely destroyed by Rita</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>With an estimated cost of $8&#160;billion in damages, Hurricane Rita\'s impact across Louisiana varied. One person is known to have drowned during the event.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NCDCLA1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCLA1-86">[86]</a></sup> Due to the hurricane\'s storm surge, which topped levees and inundated low-lying coastal communities, the greatest amount of damage extended across most of southern Louisiana, from the Mississippi River delta to the Sabine River. Widespread power outages affected roughly 1&#160;million customers, with Entergy Louisiana reporting the largest outage of 601,183 customers losing power.<sup id="cite_ref-PowerRpt4_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PowerRpt4-87">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In southeast Louisiana\'s <a href="/wiki/Terrebonne_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana">Terrebonne Parish</a>, storm surge reached 7&#160;ft (2.1&#160;m) flooding an estimated 10,000 homes. Virtually every levee was breached.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Some people were stranded in flooded communities and had to be rescued by boat. At least 100 people were reported rescued from rooftops.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Already devastated by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Canal" title="Industrial Canal">Industrial Canal</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" class="mw-redirect" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans</a> was again flooded by Hurricane Rita as the recently-and-hurriedly-repaired levees were breached once more.</p>\n<p>In south-central <a href="/wiki/Vermilion_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Vermilion Parish, Louisiana">Vermilion Parish</a>, storm surge reached all the way up to the communities of <a href="/wiki/Abbeville,_Louisiana" title="Abbeville, Louisiana">Abbeville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gueydan,_Louisiana" title="Gueydan, Louisiana">Gueydan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Arthur,_Louisiana" title="Lake Arthur, Louisiana">Lake Arthur</a>. The 10&#160;ft (3.0&#160;m) surge completely flooded <a href="/wiki/Pecan_Island,_Louisiana" title="Pecan Island, Louisiana">Pecan Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_City,_Louisiana" title="Intracoastal City, Louisiana">Intracoastal City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delcambre,_Louisiana" title="Delcambre, Louisiana">Delcambre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NCDCLA1_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCDCLA1-86">[86]</a></sup> Nearly all of the structures on Pecan Island were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup> Rescue efforts were undertaken for up to 1,000 people stranded by local flooding. On Saturday, September 24 alone, 250 people were rescued.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-90">[90]</a></sup></p>\n<p>However, the southwestern region of the state near where Rita made landfall was undeniably the worst impacted region in Louisiana.<sup id="cite_ref-TCR_2-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">Cameron Parish</a>, the damage was catastrophic, particularly along the coastline and north to the Intracoastal Waterway. Coastal storm surge was estimated around 18&#160;ft (5.5&#160;m), with lower levels farther inland from the coast, yet much of north-western and north-central Cameron Parish experienced significant flooding. The southern Cameron Parish communities of Cameron, Creole, Grand Chenier, Holly Beach, Johnson Bayou, Little Chenier and Oak Grove were either heavily devastated or entirely wiped out by the storm surge, with nearly 95 percent of homes, businesses, and infrastructure completely destroyed. Closer to the Intracoastal Waterway, communities shared a similar fate; Big Lake, Deatonville, Gibbstown and <a href="/wiki/Hackberry,_Louisiana" title="Hackberry, Louisiana">Hackberry</a> were all devastated or heavily damaged. In Hackberry, an unofficial wind gust of 180&#160;mph was recorded on a boat tied up to a local dock. Above the Intracoastal Waterway in northern Cameron Parish, damage was devastating, with the communities of Grand Lake, Hebert\'s Camp, Lowry, Pelican Point, and Sweetlake suffering from extensive flooding and wind damage. Over a decade later, many communities south of the Intracoastal Waterway are still recovering, with their populations significantly lower than pre-Rita levels.</p>\n<p>To the north in <a href="/wiki/Calcasieu_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana">Calcasieu Parish</a>, the cities and communities of <a href="/wiki/Iowa,_Louisiana" title="Iowa, Louisiana">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Charles,_Louisiana" title="Lake Charles, Louisiana">Lake Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moss_Bluff,_Louisiana" title="Moss Bluff, Louisiana">Moss Bluff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulphur,_Louisiana" title="Sulphur, Louisiana">Sulphur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Westlake,_Louisiana" title="Westlake, Louisiana">Westlake</a> suffered severe wind damage, and some areas also received flooding due to both storm surge and heavy rain. In Lake Charles, the storm surge that traveled up the Calcasieu Ship Channel from the coast was estimated to be up to 8&#160;ft (2.4&#160;m). A <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a> boat secured at the north end of the lake, and several barges secured at the Port of Lake Charles, broke free from their moorings, floating loose until running into the Interstate 10 bridge over the Calcasieu River, causing minor damage. Other areas of Lake Charles also experienced severe flooding, with reports of water rising 6\xe2\x80\x938&#160;feet, at one point inundating the lower floors of the Lake Charles Civic Center. At a hotel on a section of the <a href="/wiki/Contraband_Bayou" title="Contraband Bayou">Contraband Bayou</a> near Interstate 210 and Prien Lake Road, water reportedly rose as high as the second floor. There was extensive minor-to-major structural wind damage across the entire area, including the near-devastation of the Lake Charles Regional Airport south of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-91">[91]</a></sup> Damage to the entire region\'s electrical and communications infrastructure was severe, and authorities warned returning residents that restoration of services to some areas would take weeks to months.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_20460_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_11-19-2005_in_Louisiana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHolly Beach was almost completely leveled by Rita\'s storm surge</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the western Calcasieu parish communities of <a href="/wiki/Vinton,_Louisiana" title="Vinton, Louisiana">Vinton</a> and Starks, wind damage was also severe. The roof was torn off of the Vinton Recreation Center, and many homes were damaged by fallen trees and utility poles. Damaged utility towers made power restoration problematic, with much of the area waiting months for utilities to be restored.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Allen_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Allen Parish, Louisiana">Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beauregard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Beauregard Parish, Louisiana">Beauregard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Davis_Parish,_Louisiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeff Davis Parish, Louisiana">Jeff Davis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Vernon Parish, Louisiana">Vernon</a> parishes suffered lesser, yet still significant, degrees of wind damage and flooding damage due to heavy rain.</p>\n<p>After weakening to a tropical storm, Rita entered <a href="/wiki/DeSoto_Parish,_Louisiana" title="DeSoto Parish, Louisiana">DeSoto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caddo_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Caddo Parish, Louisiana">Caddo Parishes</a>.
